  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7e5fe2cd-2268-4e19-bd2f-67b2465566f2'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1197868870" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1197868870" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1197868870?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781862308541" href="/book/show/7557604-the-spook-s-battle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1197868870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1861108152039411382">It is time for the Spook and his apprentice to finally try to do something about the big looming problem; evil witches stronghold in the Country must be taken care of. The good news: the witches are divided into three powerful clans that are too busy with infighting to do real evil. The bad news: they already united once for a time when facing a real danger. The unbelievably bad news: the mentioned danger was represented by none other than the Spook, so there is no love lost between them and the</span>
  <span id="freeText1861108152039411382" style="display:none">It is time for the Spook and his apprentice to finally try to do something about the big looming problem; evil witches stronghold in the Country must be taken care of. The good news: the witches are divided into three powerful clans that are too busy with infighting to do real evil. The bad news: they already united once for a time when facing a real danger. The unbelievably bad news: the mentioned danger was represented by none other than the Spook, so there is no love lost between them and the witches would be ready for him this time. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426263792i/13994694._SX540_.jpg" width="380" height="250" alt="Seventh Son" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>By the way, the majority of people who saw the movie Seventh Son agree that it is much weaker than this series upon which it is based. So I only used the image above just as a nice visual aid. <br><br>Mildly disappointing would be the best description of the book. For starters, the main hero of the story Tom acted really stupid in a couple of scenes. He is usually smarter than this, but he looks completely retarded in the scenes I mentioned, even for his age: he is 14. As an example of one of these scenes without spoilers is his first meeting with Mab.<br><br>The Spook whose character I found really fascinating was mostly absent. Now that I finished the book the main question still remains: what the heck was he doing all of the time? Other than being mysterious and absent, that is. <br><br>This is the first book of the series so far without any conclusion whatsoever. The narration just... stopped at one point. I would not even call the ending a real cliffhanger. There was also a big plot hole left, enough to drive a couple of aircraft carriers through - side by side. <br><br>On the positive side, it was still a fast read. Something always bothered me: Tom is seventh son. Up to now we only got to meet his oldest brother who was kind of a minor jerk. We finally meet another brother who acts like a decent human being. Some of the mysterious past of Tom's mom is revealed as well as her legacy to her youngest son. <br><br>I gave 3 stars to this book, but it does not mean I would give up on the series; on the contrary I am eager to read the next book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1861108152039411382" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1688588672" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1688588672" />
    <a title="Tommye Turner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30506556-tommye-turner"><img alt="Tommye Turner" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1688588672?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tommye Turner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tommye Turner" href="/user/show/30506556-tommye-turner">Tommye Turner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780370328928" href="/book/show/870824.The_Spook_s_Battle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30506556-tommye-turner?shelf=children-s-fiction">children-s-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30506556-tommye-turner?shelf=fantasy-read">fantasy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1688588672" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10435441483499778709">SPOILER FREE<br/><br/>This book is the perfect example of children’s fantasy being able to accomplish something epic! When I was first reading these books as a kid, this was always my favourite. <br/><br/>So much happens! We follow Thomas, Alice, and the Spook to Pendle, and as we all know, Pendle is crawling with witches. The set up of the three clans, the map of Pendle, and the influx of new characters and creatures is outstanding. Reading about the inter-clan politics and learning about new creatures, lore, and </span>
  <span id="freeText10435441483499778709" style="display:none">SPOILER FREE<br /><br />This book is the perfect example of children’s fantasy being able to accomplish something epic! When I was first reading these books as a kid, this was always my favourite. <br /><br />So much happens! We follow Thomas, Alice, and the Spook to Pendle, and as we all know, Pendle is crawling with witches. The set up of the three clans, the map of Pendle, and the influx of new characters and creatures is outstanding. Reading about the inter-clan politics and learning about new creatures, lore, and mythology, while simultaneously following a terrifying story is exactly what you get with this fourth entry in Joseph Delaney’s The Wardstone Chronicles. <br /><br />Thomas really starts to come into his own. For plot reasons, Thomas has to be separated from the Spook a lot so we can see him develop under extreme pressure, and he does just that. He faces witches, a creepy spider-like blood-sucking creature, and the most terrifying threats he has ever had to face before. He’s in over his head and he knows it, but that doesn’t stop him fighting for what is right, as well as fighting to survive.<br /><br />The story with Alice is intriguing as she is a witch, and now has to face the life she left behind. It’s fascinating to see how she copes with the temptation and threats from the Dark. <br /><br />This is the book where this series really starts to become huge in scale. The first three books introduce us to the main characters, the magic-system/lore/mythology, and foreshadows threats to come. The Spook’s Battle is where those elements come together and create an epic start for an epic series. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10435441483499778709" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_172866365" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/172866365" />
    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/172866365?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer172866365" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3109270413335125152">Up to this point I've liked this series, and I didn't really "dislike" this one. It was however a bit "waring" before it tied up.<br/><br/>One of my friends here on Goodreads observed that her only complaint with the series was that Tom didn't develop... At the time I was only 3 books in and took the view I'd wait and see. So far I'd only covered about a year in Tom's life. This is the 4th book in the series, and right out of the gate (so to speak) Tom pretty much makes the same mistake he made in the fir</span>
  <span id="freeText3109270413335125152" style="display:none">Up to this point I've liked this series, and I didn't really "dislike" this one. It was however a bit "waring" before it tied up.<br /><br />One of my friends here on Goodreads observed that her only complaint with the series was that Tom didn't develop... At the time I was only 3 books in and took the view I'd wait and see. So far I'd only covered about a year in Tom's life. This is the 4th book in the series, and right out of the gate (so to speak) Tom pretty much makes the same mistake he made in the first volume.<br /><br />Oh well.<br /><br />This volume attempts a somewhat more involved plot and tries to tell a slightly more intricate story. It only "sort of" succeeds. Without spoilers and being cognizant that this is my opinion, I'll say that the story stumbles about more than the prior novels. It didn't hold my interest and I was ready for it to end. The "hook" of the novel, the Fiend of the title works more as a threat hanging over this book and then as a set up for what's to come in later volumes.<br /><br />How a younger reader will like this book I'd hesitate to say. Again, be aware that the plot points in this book deal with murder, consuming human blood, child murder also witches and "other things" that can look into other's houses through mirrors. This could all be a bit much for younger children. That aside however, the fact that I and older readers will see plot points coming a few miles off may not be as big an issue for younger readers who haven't read the plots that often before.<br /><br />They may however by now (if they are following the series) note that Tom seems to be pretty thick in that he placed himself in the soup...again.<br /><br />So, not as good as the previous volumes slightly more tedious and slightly disjointed. I have the next book(s) from the library here already so I plan to follow through at least one more volume. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3109270413335125152" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/987105680?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard" href="/user/show/8386404-richard">Richard</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer987105680" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12056127227122360967">7.5/10<br/><br/>Another enjoyable outing in this series which keeps on impressing. This is the fourth in the series and each one has been consistently good. The only negative I could say is that there hasn’t been a great deal of character development throughout but for the type of books these are and the audience they are aimed at (i.e. not me) you can’t really knock it. They seem to follow a similar formula in each one but if it ain’t broke don’t fix it.<br/><br/>The stakes are raised somewhat in this outing with </span>
  <span id="freeText12056127227122360967" style="display:none">7.5/10<br /><br />Another enjoyable outing in this series which keeps on impressing. This is the fourth in the series and each one has been consistently good. The only negative I could say is that there hasn’t been a great deal of character development throughout but for the type of books these are and the audience they are aimed at (i.e. not me) you can’t really knock it. They seem to follow a similar formula in each one but if it ain’t broke don’t fix it.<br /><br />The stakes are raised somewhat in this outing with Tom, the Spooks Apprentice, facing off against 3 Witch clans who are all trying to bring back the Devil to earth. Tom, the Spook and their trusty witch Alice are on the hunt to try and stop this from happening because it would put a real crimp in your day having to fight the devil instead of some pesky witches. We learn a lot more about Tom’s mam and where he comes from throughout this which does add an extra dimension to the story and we also learn about the witch assassin Grimalkin who is destined to turn up in the next few novels. <br /><br />Even though these are aimed at a younger audience (think early teens) I still find myself enjoying them and reading them quite quickly. The overall setting is one of the highlights for me in this series as are the descriptions of the actual locations visited in each outing, in this case Pendle. You get the sense that something is brewing with an overall plot arc ready to come into view sooner rather than later which keeps your attention also. An enjoyable read and I will look forward to picking up the next one in the series. <br /><br />If you like this try: “Magyk” by Angie Sage</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137296530?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karissa" href="/user/show/4057501-karissa">Karissa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137296530" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17084986768030729213">This is the 4th book in the Last Apprentice series by Joseph Delaney. Wow was this an excellent book!<br/><br/>After hearing over and over about how bad things are in Pindle; Tom and the Spook are finally going to go there to deal with the witch problem for good. Alice is along to help them, using all her witchy knowledge for good. Nothing goes as planned though when the witches strike first at the place Tom is most vulnerable. Will they be able to root out all the witches? Will the witches raise the devi</span>
  <span id="freeText17084986768030729213" style="display:none">This is the 4th book in the Last Apprentice series by Joseph Delaney. Wow was this an excellent book!<br /><br />After hearing over and over about how bad things are in Pindle; Tom and the Spook are finally going to go there to deal with the witch problem for good. Alice is along to help them, using all her witchy knowledge for good. Nothing goes as planned though when the witches strike first at the place Tom is most vulnerable. Will they be able to root out all the witches? Will the witches raise the devil himself? What is in the trunks Mam left Tom? Exactly who is Mam? All of these questions are answered to some extent.<br /><br />This was a wonderfully written book; as usual. It may be one of the best books in this series yet. It is very suspenseful and spooky, there is lots of action (more than usual). Alice's character is being developed nicely and Tom really comes into his own in this book. We get to meet more of Tom's brothers; and the future looks bleaker than ever. This is the first book where the greater outside world really starts to have an influence on what is happening to Tom. Usually the books are pretty isolated to a small area, but not this one, things are more dire than ever.<br /><br />It was just a great book. I was disappointed when I was finished. These are so fun to read and so well written. I love them and cannot wait to get my hands on the next one!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17084986768030729213" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="I&#39;mogén" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23443295-i-mog-n"><img alt="I&#39;mogén" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542116512p2/23443295.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="I&#39;mogén" class="user" itemprop="url" name="I&#39;mogén" href="/user/show/23443295-i-mog-n">I&#39;mogén</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781782952480" href="/book/show/18457325-the-spook-s-battle">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1585109912" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2048095537732810771">The Spook's Battle, the fourth book in The Wardstone Chronicles, was action packed and fast paced, whilst still being very plot driven and fun to read. In saying that, it still fell short of the 4 star rating that I gave the other books, as I wasn't completely absorbed as I had been before. However, the 3 stars I've given it is considered a high 3.<br/><br/>The cover was really creepy and mirrors what the story tells within, because pretty much from the first few pages I was over come with a feeling of dr</span>
  <span id="freeText2048095537732810771" style="display:none">The Spook's Battle, the fourth book in The Wardstone Chronicles, was action packed and fast paced, whilst still being very plot driven and fun to read. In saying that, it still fell short of the 4 star rating that I gave the other books, as I wasn't completely absorbed as I had been before. However, the 3 stars I've given it is considered a high 3.<br /><br />The cover was really creepy and mirrors what the story tells within, because pretty much from the first few pages I was over come with a feeling of dread! It was an increasingly dangerous time for the County and I knew that bad things were bound to happen!<br /><br />Tom's luck really seemed to turn for the worst in this installment, and I was always left wondering "WHERE THE HELL IS GREGGORY!?". Seeing Tom fending off the dark on his own though was really inspiring to see and gave him further depth and development. <br /><br />I liked the introduction to another family member of Tom's and more characters in general as it put more weight on the risk of Tom failing against evil!<br /><br />The contents of Mam's trunks were such a surprise!! <br /><br />There was a gollum like character in this that was really creepy and some of the prophecies it spoke were really unsettling!<br /><br />One thing that annoyed me about the book is that some locations seemed far away at one point and then seemingly close when it was convinent, so I lost a sence of destination length. <br /><br />Finally, I really enjoyed Alice's entry at the back and all the new things Tom learned. I feel like there was so much more detail in his diary, this time around.<br /><br />Pick it up, give it a go and enjoy! &gt;(^_^)&lt; <br />Gén</span>

<div id="review_473398137" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/473398137" />
    <a title="Duffy Pratt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2729963-duffy-pratt"><img alt="Duffy Pratt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1282095213p2/2729963.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/473398137?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Duffy Pratt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Duffy Pratt" href="/user/show/2729963-duffy-pratt">Duffy Pratt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2729963-duffy-pratt?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2729963-duffy-pratt?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2729963-duffy-pratt?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer473398137" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15887382836941015703">Another solid installment in the continuing adventures of Tom Ward. This book worked less well as a stand-alone, mostly because the characters mainly fail to achieve the goals they set for themselves at the beginning. And when there is success, it comes more from some outside agency than from the initiative of the characters themselves.<br/><br/>The other thing that bothered me here was, for the first time, I think this book suffered from the "Red Shirt of Death" syndrome. I get the feeling that the last </span>
  <span id="freeText15887382836941015703" style="display:none">Another solid installment in the continuing adventures of Tom Ward. This book worked less well as a stand-alone, mostly because the characters mainly fail to achieve the goals they set for themselves at the beginning. And when there is success, it comes more from some outside agency than from the initiative of the characters themselves.<br /><br />The other thing that bothered me here was, for the first time, I think this book suffered from the "Red Shirt of Death" syndrome. I get the feeling that the last thing anyone should want to be is an old friend of the Spook's at the start of one of these books.<br /><br />Once again, I thought the writing was straightforward and solid. The characters are staying true to themselves for the most part. In this book, Tom comes across as a bit stupider than in the earlier ones, but to a certain extent that may just be the combination of awakening hormones and the "glamour" that witches use on him. There are at least two times when Tom should have been much more wary that he is. His tendency to rush off to try to help people by himself is part of his character. But by now he should have enough experience to know that he often needs help.<br /><br />All in all, I thought this was a slight step down from the last two books, but its still quite good, and I'm looking forward to getting my copy of the next one, hopefully before Christmas.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15887382836941015703" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Woodge" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Woodge" href="/user/show/1063661-woodge">Woodge</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1063661-woodge?shelf=kids">kids</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1063661-woodge?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1063661-woodge?shelf=reading-aloud">reading-aloud</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer164317902" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16096924794998768582">I've been reading this aloud to Luke (age 9) for the past several weeks. We took a break here and there, but last night we had to read the final 50 pages all at once. We've been really enjoying this series (which currently numbers about 8 books). Sometimes I wonder if it's a bit too creepy for Luke but he's been digging it. After finishing this one he said, "Let's start the next book tomorrow night!" So far I think this book might be my favorite out of the series so far. In this story our three </span>
  <span id="freeText16096924794998768582" style="display:none">I've been reading this aloud to Luke (age 9) for the past several weeks. We took a break here and there, but last night we had to read the final 50 pages all at once. We've been really enjoying this series (which currently numbers about 8 books). Sometimes I wonder if it's a bit too creepy for Luke but he's been digging it. After finishing this one he said, "Let's start the next book tomorrow night!" So far I think this book might be my favorite out of the series so far. In this story our three heroes, Tom (the last apprentice), the Spook (his master, John Gregory), and Alice (a young girl descended from a witch clan) face off against three covens of witches in the town of Pendle. They are trying to put aside their differences long enough to bring the Fiend over from the dark into our world. And the Fiend is no less than Old Nick himself. One of the things I like about this series is that even though there are priests in the story, the religious aspects are toned down and impartial. It's not assumed that you the reader, or a certain character is a believer. In fact, there are characters of every stripe. It's well done. And the wood-cut illustrations that begin every chapter are very cool too. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16096924794998768582" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12240725301841771567">I finished writing this review and it got eaten by the computer gremlins. Oh well, here it goes again. I listened to this on audiobook while I was packing up the house this summer, and it greatly improved what was a tedious task. The narration is well done. This series is pretty darn spooky, no pun intended. It's downright scary at times. The narrator lends well to the atmosphere. There's a feeling of the monster lurking in the dark behind every closed door, a sense of paranoia and an urgency no</span>
  <span id="freeText12240725301841771567" style="display:none">I finished writing this review and it got eaten by the computer gremlins. Oh well, here it goes again. I listened to this on audiobook while I was packing up the house this summer, and it greatly improved what was a tedious task. The narration is well done. This series is pretty darn spooky, no pun intended. It's downright scary at times. The narrator lends well to the atmosphere. There's a feeling of the monster lurking in the dark behind every closed door, a sense of paranoia and an urgency not to trust anyone. The storyline enhances that feeling because the monsters lurk in human form. More of the witches storyline in this one, and further development of the relationship between Tom and Alice. Definitely worth a read.</span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/82054927?book_show_action=true">Dec 25, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrick" href="/user/show/881570-patrick">Patrick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780060891299" href="/book/show/6282141-attack-of-the-fiend">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/881570-patrick?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer82054927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17273765060058509596">I'm souring on this series. The characters once again are meh. There is finally a sympathetic religious character, but he ends up being a naive weakling who loses his faith when being killed by an unnatural kid monster. Despite that, the "fiend" of the title is the devil himself being loosed by some angry witches. I like the overarching story of a greater light/dark battle than just the county coming more fully into the plot, but I'm just not liking the characters or the tone. Without exception,</span>
  <span id="freeText17273765060058509596" style="display:none">I'm souring on this series. The characters once again are meh. There is finally a sympathetic religious character, but he ends up being a naive weakling who loses his faith when being killed by an unnatural kid monster. Despite that, the "fiend" of the title is the devil himself being loosed by some angry witches. I like the overarching story of a greater light/dark battle than just the county coming more fully into the plot, but I'm just not liking the characters or the tone. Without exception, the "regular" characters, townspeople, farmers, etc., are blind to obvious magical stuff going on around them and religion is a weak crutch to ignore the crazy evil magic stuff happening. <br /><br />And while I love Alice in concept, she and the main kid almost never hold real conversations. They just hold hands and know they have a future together despite having nothing in common besides supernatural abilities and interests in the unseen. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17273765060058509596" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5078500061017728174">I always get excited when I find that Delaney has written another book for the Last Apprentice series. I also get worried. How can he write about the same thing and have it not get boring? Well Delaney pulls it off every time. I am always on the edge of my seat throughout the whole book. He has a wonderful way of writing that doesn't slow down a bit. I have loved every book in this series (including this one). My 2 kids love them as well. <br/>This time the Spook and Tom do not have to fight a witch </span>
  <span id="freeText5078500061017728174" style="display:none">I always get excited when I find that Delaney has written another book for the Last Apprentice series. I also get worried. How can he write about the same thing and have it not get boring? Well Delaney pulls it off every time. I am always on the edge of my seat throughout the whole book. He has a wonderful way of writing that doesn't slow down a bit. I have loved every book in this series (including this one). My 2 kids love them as well. <br />This time the Spook and Tom do not have to fight a witch or two but instead three whole covens. That sounds bad enough but put in the Fiend as well... let's just say they have a lot of ground to cover. On top of that Tom finds himself alone many times and having to put to test what the Spook has taught him. Can such a short apprenticeship and his wits be enough? Read the book and find out. I guarantee you won't be disappointed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5078500061017728174" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer16156638490795271298">The fourth installment of The Last Apprentice, Attack of the Fiend, picks up shortly after Night of the Soul Stealer, young Tomas Ward continuing his studies in the way of the Spook, that shunned wanderer who faces off against the gruesome creatures that stalk the night. Now, he and his master are making their way to Pendle, where for years now three witch clans have terrorized the area, and as they make their way there, it becomes apparent that the three clans are planning something truly sinis</span>
  <span id="freeText16156638490795271298" style="display:none">The fourth installment of The Last Apprentice, Attack of the Fiend, picks up shortly after Night of the Soul Stealer, young Tomas Ward continuing his studies in the way of the Spook, that shunned wanderer who faces off against the gruesome creatures that stalk the night. Now, he and his master are making their way to Pendle, where for years now three witch clans have terrorized the area, and as they make their way there, it becomes apparent that the three clans are planning something truly sinister for the upcoming Lammas. With the Spook and his friend Alice, Tom will face off against succubi and bloodsuckers alike as he tries to stop hell itself from being loosed upon the world, as well as learning things about his mother he could never had dreamed of. <br /><br />Joseph Delaney weaves a thoroughly enjoyable tale that will without fail entertain both young and old. While I felt it was a bit drier that the the previous ones, Attack of the Fiend remains filled with magic and suspense and opens up whole new possibilities for future installments. </span>

Looking forward to starting the next book soon :)<br /><br />Love the audio narration too!</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2502275734" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11213318065842727">I really enjoyed this Fantasy book. The story takes place in a fictional town called chimpenden where a spook (ghost Hunter) and his apprentice live. They have to go to a another town to fight witches and to make it safe for people to live there. I really liked it that the author never left me bored and always eager to keep reading or to get back to the book. I was always excited to read the book. I really like both of the characters because they had to make so many important or life threatening</span>
  <span id="freeText11213318065842727" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this Fantasy book. The story takes place in a fictional town called chimpenden where a spook (ghost Hunter) and his apprentice live. They have to go to a another town to fight witches and to make it safe for people to live there. I really liked it that the author never left me bored and always eager to keep reading or to get back to the book. I was always excited to read the book. I really like both of the characters because they had to make so many important or life threatening decisions that I could never see my self making. i also liked it how they weren't selfish and always helped people before they would help themselves. Overall a really good book and series.</span>

<div id="review_3222188492" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3222188492" />
    <a title="Jodie &quot;Bookish&quot;  Cook" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62766804-jodie-bookish-cook"><img alt="Jodie &quot;Bookish&quot;  Cook" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1482373682p2/62766804.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3222188492?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jodie &quot;Bookish&quot;  Cook" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jodie &quot;Bookish&quot;  Cook" href="/user/show/62766804-jodie-bookish-cook">Jodie &quot;Bookish&quot;  Cook</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780370328928" href="/book/show/870824.The_Spook_s_Battle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62766804-jodie-bookish-cook?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62766804-jodie-bookish-cook?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3222188492&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3222188492" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer908333230937364572">Book Review <br/>Title: The Spook’s Battle (The Wardstone Chronicles #4)<br/>Author: Joseph Delaney <br/>Genre: YA/Paranormal/Fantasy<br/>Rating: *****<br/>Review: So as I mentioned in my previous review; Night of the Soulstealer, I am switching to the UK titles and covers as they are easier for me to use than the US ones. If you would like to review the previous 3 reviews, search for The Last Apprentice. The Spook’s Battle is the fourth book in the Wardstone Chronicles and I can’t wait for these series to get going in </span>
  <span id="freeText908333230937364572" style="display:none">Book Review <br />Title: The Spook’s Battle (The Wardstone Chronicles #4)<br />Author: Joseph Delaney <br />Genre: YA/Paranormal/Fantasy<br />Rating: *****<br />Review: So as I mentioned in my previous review; Night of the Soulstealer, I am switching to the UK titles and covers as they are easier for me to use than the US ones. If you would like to review the previous 3 reviews, search for The Last Apprentice. The Spook’s Battle is the fourth book in the Wardstone Chronicles and I can’t wait for these series to get going in earnest now because we have been introduced to all our main characters, we’ve seen their relationships develop especially between Alice and Tom, and also between Tom and Mr. Gregory who we know is going to be leaving the series soon as his health and age are causing his strength to fail. This is also the first book in the series where I will be listening to the audiobook as well as reading along with the physical copy. The opening of the Spook’s Battle was interesting, we see Tom and Alice training in preparation for their trip to Pendle. This trip is going to be their most dangerous yet as Pendle is a place where witches live and there are 3 main clans there, who previously cursed the Spook. Tom has now been with Mr. Gregory a year and he is know learning all about witches but Mr. Gregory tells him to be wary as there are some abilities or types of witches that he might not have encountered before, so they will have to learn as they go. Mr. Gregory is expecting a visitor so he is sending Alice and Tom back to his family farm to collect the trunks his mother left him. <br />As they get close to his family far, Tom is excited to see Jack, Ellie and Mary again but he is also said that his parents won’t be there but with Alice he has some comfort. This is quickly destroyed when they find the barn has burned down and the house empty but his mother’s chests are also missing, Alice can smell that witches have been there recently and thinks that they used Jack to get into his mother’s room and remove the chest, so they must have something very important inside them and the family would have been taken back to Pendle with them. The pair decide Alice should go on to Pendle as it won’t be bad if she is caught as she has family there and Tom should head back to Mr. Gregory and tell him what happened which is exactly what they do. Mr. Gregory explains that the Malkin clan and the Deane clan have joined forces and are trying to get the Mouldheel clan to join them before the witch sabbath of Lammas on the 1st of August and Mr. Gregory is scared that Jack and his family are being held there for a special reason and they set out for Pendle at once. Tom is terrified that something is going to happen to his family but he is also aware that his master wants to deal with the Pendle witches once and for all so this mission is extremely dangerous for them all. <br />As we approach the ¼ mark in the novel, both Tom and Mr. Gregory have arrived in Pendle and after a brief catch up with his former apprentice turned priest Father Stocks both head out looking for information on Tom’s family leaving him with the task of cleaning up the graveyard which is where he meets Mab. Mab tells Tom that Alice as sent her as she is spellbound and needs help, Tom being the gentle soul he is agrees to go with her but he knows something isn’t right about the situation. Mab leads him to a meeting place where her twin sisters are waiting and Tom realises that this is a meeting place for a coven of witches. The girls insists on playing a game of truth or dare and Mab tries to bind Tom to her with a kiss, however, Tom remembers where Alice dug her nails into him, scarring him and binding him to her which allows him to break Man’s spell over him and he proclaims to her that he belongs to Alice and her alone. This enrages Mab, who tells him her full name is Mab Mouldheel and that she intends to make Tom hers the second she kills Alice. Tom knows that Alice must be their prisoner and rather than going back for Mr. Gregory as he is doubtful whether he had even returned and Alice’s life is on the line, he decides to go after the Mouldheel sisters alone to rescue his friend. He manages to find Alice but not before the witches uses the mirrors inform the others and there are now a pack of witches hot on their heels but luckily for them they comes across a dead witch named Maggie Malkin, a cousin of Alice’s and she sets the on the Mouldheels. However, Alice tells Tom that she learned two days ago his family was alive but they are being held in the pits underneath Malkin Tower and her family are right in the middle of whatever is going on. We have also learned that Father Stocks believes that something is driving the clans together in order to summon the Fiend, the Devil himself back to the Earth to usher in a new age of darkness.<br />As we cross the ¼ mark in the novel, Tom and Alice return to Father Stock’s home where they relay all the details to Mr. Gregory but Tom deliberately omits that Alice spoke to the dead witch, Maggie because he knows his master wouldn’t approve of this and would distrust Alice even more. Alice also provides information on a seer named Tibb who say the chests that belonged to Tom’s mother and knew there was something in them they needed to get their hands on. It seems that the witches manages to open the smaller ones but can’t get into the three larger ones. Father Stocks and Mr. Gregory know there is no way they can get into Malkin Tower and rescue Tom’s family as they number only four and they don’t know how many witches are in the tower or how powerful they are, Father Stocks suggests they involve the local law enforcement who can get into the Tower as he doesn’t believe in witchcraft. Father Stocks and Tom make the short journey to Read Hall and initially meet the housekeeper Mistress Wurmalde and Tom instantly recognises her as a dark witch but he can’t say anything, even when they talk to the magistrate Tom is concerned they are being spied on in the mirror. As they make their way to Malkin Tower, Tom grows more and more anxious that news has already been passed to the witches inside and how is family is coping. They aren’t successful in gaining entry to the Tower but the magistrate is going to get an army garrison to get inside and Father Stocks and Tom return to Read Hall but Tom isn’t comfortable about returning but Father Stocks calms him. As soon as he enters his room Tom turns the mirror around so he can’t be spied on and he is determined not to sleep, this pays off as he spots a carriage leaving Read Hall and suspects that Mistress Wurmalde is inside and decides to wait to see when she returns.<br />As we approach the halfway mark in the novel, Wurmalde has given Tom one day and one night to think about her proposition to give him the keys to his mother’s trunks in exchange for the lives on his family. She tells him that Ellie lost the baby she was carrying, Mary screams with her nightmares and Jack has been driven slightly mad by entering his mother’s room possibly because he was betraying his brother in doing it. We learn that Jack had a copy of the key made which is how he was able to get into the room in the first place. Neither Tom nor Father Stocks is safe in the house as they soon learn as Wurmalde brough Tibb back with her and after feeding from Father Stock he tells Tom something about his future, a girl he will love and will betray him but ultimately die for him and I am sure this is Alice he is talking about. Tom bluffing tell Tibb he knows what is in the chest and when he demands to know what it is, he speaks words he knows to be true but they don’t belong to him and I think they belong to his mother, and he says the death of the Pendle clans lies within the trunks. It seems that Wurmalde, a former enemy of his mother’s, can’t take the keys from him they need to be given, no doubt the work of his mothers. In the daylight hours he escape to get Mr. Gregory but he isn’t there so he and Alice return to Read Hall but on the way she tells him Mab left a message for him, she will get him into Malkin Tower and help rescue his family in exchange for the keys and while he initially refuses it is Alice that points out Mab would be in as much danger as them so she would lie about being able to get them in or out undetected and that the pair of them could easily overpower her alone and he agrees. Upon returning to Read Hall, Tom enters first telling Alice to follow but when he enters Father Stock’s room he is dead with a dagger in his chest and Wurmalde has framed him as a thief and murderer. Tom sits alone in a cell as midnight approaches, the deadline Wurmalde had given and when she returns for an answer, he refuses to give up the keys. Tom knows he has sacrificed his family who are going to end up in the hands of Grimalkin, the Malkin clan’s assassin and for the first time he regrets becoming the Spook’s apprentice and weeps.<br />As we cross into the second half of the novel, Tom is praying that Alice and Mr. Gregory will arrive soon and rescue him and hopes that there might still be time to save his family. This doesn’t happen but the army are trying to blast their way into Malkin Tower with the aid of a cannon but work has to be stopped until the following day. Immediately the men fall asleep and a horde of witches descend upon Tom but they are led by Mab who has Alice with her, she frees him so they can bargain so for the trunks, Tom has no intention of giving them up but agrees, nonetheless. Mab lead him and Alice to the secret entrance to Malkin Tower where dead Maggie has been chained but in a brief moment, she whispers something to Alice that Tom knows will help them. As they descend both Alice and Mab sniff out something unpleasant but Tom has his staff which Alice kept hold of so at least he has a weapon that he can use against whatever it is that is guarding the tunnels beneath the Tower. After dealing with the wight that guards the passageway, the final reach the lower levels of the cells which only house ghosts and bones, moving up a level to the only other level of cells time is running out as they need the candle to get past the wight again but in the third cell Tom checks he finds Mary and Ellie. Now together Tom knows the danger he has put his family in but he can’t dwell on it for long as Jack needs to be carried as he is unresponsive. They think about taking him into the tunnels but Mab scryed their journey and knows if they stay put the soldiers will breach the castle causing the witches to flee through the tunnel. She also knows two are going to come back, she and Alice swiftly deal with them and they are free to go above to get out of the Tower but Mab leads them first to the room where Tom’s trunks are held. <br />As we approach the ¾ mark in the novel, Tom realises a little too late that he has been played by Mab who has seen what was going to happen and used it all to her advantage. As she threatens Mary’s life, Tom has no choice to hand over the keys but when Mab tries to use them, they won’t open the trunks. Inside on of the books there is a letter addressed to Tom from his mother, the letter tells him that inside the two trunks are her sisters who can only be awakened by the light of the moon by his own hand. Tom tells Mab that they need to be opened under the moon but leaves out what is inside and very quickly the two lamia witches awaken and set themselves upon the Mouldheels but leave Tom alone as he shares their blood. Mab swears that she is going to join Wurmalde now to help raise the Devil and then she is going to send him after Tom and he knows he has possibly put everyone in the County in danger. While the lamias as awake Tom has very little to do with them as he doesn’t want to face the fact he is half witch just yet and he also wonders where Mr. Gregory is as he still hasn’t arrived. Alone in the Tower apart from his aunts, Tom isn’t sure what to do but the following day Alice, Mr. Gregory and his brother James arrive at the Tower and they begins to put a plan in place to deal with the witches especially Wurmalde as she seems to be the one leading everything. However, as Alice and the Spook sleep, Tom and James talk and Tom reads from one of his mother diaries that James opened to the page that describes his birth and his mothers prediction that he would become a blacksmith, which he did. James tells Tom he is going to move home to support Jack and Ellie as his mother asked him to do at their father’s funeral and Tom begins to wonder whether his mother had seen all this before they were even born and he thinks that somehow she is still helping them from afar. However, Tom doesn’t tell anyone that his mother’s letter told him that the Fiend would take flesh once more meaning despite their plan they are going to fail in stopping the Lammas ritual the witches are planning and that the County will be plunged into darkness. <br />As we cross into the final section of the novel, James sets out to collect the villagers ready to help them stop the witches while Tom and his Master set out to deal with Wurmalde but not before Tom and Alice retrieve his family returning them to the safety of the Tower. Alice is left behind with the lamias in order to defend the Tower in their absence. As the head to Read Hall something isn’t right, inside they find the magistrate dead and Tibb in the cellar. Tibb is dying anyway and he tells Tom that Wurmalde has abandoned him and that she will raise the Fiend and he will serve her for only two days to complete her mission of killing Tom before he strikes out on his own path. He tells Tom of his mother how she once belonged to the dark and faltered which is why she was bound to the rock where his father saved her. After that she was torn between darkness and light and after failing to kill his dad she turned completely to the light but Tibb claims she has returned to it now with his father’s death and Tom refuses to believe that. Mr. Gregory makes short work of killing Tibb and they decide to return to the Tower as hunting Wurmalde down would take too much time and it would be better to go after the covens directly before Lammas. <br /><br />full review at forthenovellovers.wordpress.com</span>
  <a data-text-id="908333230937364572" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4656215466027272378">*SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS*<br/><br/><br/>1. A very brief highlight or summary of the book. Where did the story take place (setting)? Who are the main and minor characters in the book?<br/> In this part of the series, Tom was sent to be trained by Arkwright for combat skills as his formal spook is much too</span>
  <span id="freeText4656215466027272378" style="display:none">*SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS**SPOILERS*<br /><br /><br />1. A very brief highlight or summary of the book. Where did the story take place (setting)? Who are the main and minor characters in the book?<br /> In this part of the series, Tom was sent to be trained by Arkwright for combat skills as his formal spook is much too old for such things. It was a rough start for Tom but it was ok but for not that long. It was soon after that the three deadly witch clans have allied together to summon only one thing. The fiend. Tom has to stop the fiend and potentially destroy the world. Although the fiend could kill Tom easily, that would mean his time in this world would soon end if he did that. Therefore, he has sent out his daughters to kill Tom and continue on with his destruction. The main characters are Tom Ward, Alice, Gregory(spook), and the new character, Arkwright.<br />2. Do the characters in the book seem believable or do they seem real (characterization)? Explain how and why. Use the character traits listed below to help:<br /> Yes I think they are very real. The reason I think this was because each and every character has a very unique personality. For example Arkwright, seemed very strict with Tom and was a VERY heavy drinker. But Tom was a decent boy who was shy at times but very clever. This is why I think they are real and it really affects how the story escalates. <br />3. Appearance: What does the main character look like in your mind? I think that Tom Ward is a fourteen year old teenager with brown hair and brown eyes. He may be pretty short but very decent strength.<br /><br />4. Speech: What do the characters say that tells a reader something about their character? “Give me a memorable quote from the novel then explain the significance of this quote to the reader of the document.”<br /> Something that the fiend said in the story is that, “You will be betrayed by one of my daughters.”. Since the fiend had some daughters to kill Tom, one of Tom’s friends was a witch and a powerful one. In the previous books, Tom has been warned that someone will betray him over and over which was very strange. But from what the Fiend said, it shows just how powerful of a monster he is. Not to mention the death trail of cadavers everywhere in the county.<br />5. Action: What do the characters “do” that tells a reader something about their character? What do their actions tells us about them as a person?<br /> Several times in the book, when Tom got in trouble by Arkwright and when he disciplines the boy, I can say that he gets very very angry to him. He would pretty much get close to his face and say something like “Don’t ever do that again. Understand me?”. From this, although he may be a trained spook and saves the day and all, he can be very very grumpy. <br />6. Did you like the book, and most importantly, why did you like the book? Or did you not like the book, and most importantly, why didn’t you like the book?<br /> Well I didn’t really like the book since it was very slow. It was just Tom’s training to become a spook which took up almost half the book until you got to the good stuff. I just wished the author could just skip a couple parts like after two weeks. But what bothered me most was the sloppy illustrations of the cursive. In the book there would be sent letters to Tom that he would read and I pretty much skipped those since it just gave me a real headache. Other than that, the story was kind of good and I give it a 8/10<br />7. What was or is the theme of the novel and give me a specific example of how you came to the determination of this theme. What specifically happened in the novel that makes you believe that your theme is a correct one?<br /> Despite Arkwright’s actions toward Tom Ward, I think the theme of this story is to always listen to adults. Several times Tom was warned not to do this or do that yet Tom was convinced by his curiosity. But there’s also a lesson for Arkwright too. If they do it when you told them not to, it’s not the end of the world. You don’t have to get up all in their face saying almost death threats to them. If they make a mistake, correct them and be professional. What I think why these two themes really standed out was because, like in the several books, Tom would often disobey his master and get in trouble. But not the way Arkwright would do it. When he got in trouble by his master, he wouldn’t get a spanking just like that. This is why these theme’s really standed out to me.<br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_79137004" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/79137004" />
    <a title="Amelia, free market Puritan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan"><img alt="Amelia, free market Puritan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508223427p2/1852293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/79137004?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amelia, free market Puritan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amelia, free market Puritan" href="/user/show/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan">Amelia, free market Puritan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780370328928" href="/book/show/870824.The_Spook_s_Battle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=ya-kids-teen">ya-kids-teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=series-books">series-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=point-of-view-guy">point-of-view-guy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer79137004" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7850572529782271420">This is definitely the axis book around which the series will start to evolve… and it’s about time, too – holy cow, this is book #4!<br/><br/>I felt like The Spook’s Battle in particular was a long time coming. Why? Well, we finally start to piece together Alice’s background, and we also get hands-on dealings with the most malevolent witches in the County! After hearing about them for the better part of 3 books, I was excited to actually see them. We also get more insight into Tom’s family dynamics, inclu</span>
  <span id="freeText7850572529782271420" style="display:none">This is definitely the axis book around which the series will start to evolve… and it’s about time, too – holy cow, this is book #4!<br /><br />I felt like The Spook’s Battle in particular was a long time coming. Why? Well, we finally start to piece together Alice’s background, and we also get hands-on dealings with the most malevolent witches in the County! After hearing about them for the better part of 3 books, I was excited to actually see them. We also get more insight into Tom’s family dynamics, including his mysterious mother and her quickly-unraveling past… interesting! <br />- The pacing of the overall series is starting to get on my nerves – the last 4 books have taken place roughly over a year’s time…that is waaaaaay to slow (in my opinion, at least). I said this in the review for <i>The Spook’s Secret</i>: I’m ready for Tom to start growing up! He’s matured so much emotionally, yes, but he still functions like a young kid... Alice is starting to slightly surpass Tom as my favorite character! She’s quite the underdog, though: nobody trusts her and everybody is just waiting for her to screw up. Now granted, she is a witch with a shady past, but come on, give her a break! It’s like your Typical Girl scenario: you’ve got a problem, but for some reason the menfolk can’t seem to get their act together and solve the problem, so you do it, then they jump on you because they don’t like your methods! Poor Alice! I can certainly relate, haha. <br />- One thing Delaney does really, really well is “connect-the-dots”. I love it when a series author finds ways to reiterate certain points from previous books into the current book. There were quite a lot of things from <i>Apprentice</i> and <i>Curse</i>, for example, that I managed to forget, so it was good of Delaney to remind me how everything relates to each other. The only thing I’m unsure about is his order-of-events. For example, he had a really good “recap” conversation between two characters where you as the reader are given an explanation for something that happened earlier on in the series – however, this conversation occurs at the very end of the story, so you go through 300+ pages of “WHAT THE?!?!?!” before you get your answer. To me, that’s not really suspense, that’s distracting. If I’m paying so much attention to a particular unexplained plot point, and I’m given no “hold-your-horses, I’ll-get-to-the-explanation-later” from the author (and authors do give you clues that they’re not going to leave you hanging – JK Rowling, for example) it becomes hard for me to concentrate on the rest of the story. Maybe that’s just me, though… So bottom line: Delaney does tie up loose ends and tie in his previous stories with the present one, he just does it at weird times…<br />- Another thing I really like about Delaney and this series: his creativity at times gets off-the-charts. No, he didn’t “create” boggarts, wights, and witches, but he puts his own personal touches on creatures and legends you thought you knew already, and the result is near-constant surprise on part of the reader. I was certainly impressed. On the other hand: the last 3 books in a row have pretty much used the same idea when it comes to your “creature of the dark” – a malevolent, spirit thing that has been/could be mistaken for some kind of godlike being. The Bane. Golgoth. The Fiend. I want something more original, please. Just having the three covens of evil witches would have sufficed, at least in my opinion. And that brings me to my next point: <br />- This series is starting to move in the “philosophical direction” and I’m not sure how I feel about that. For one thing, I don’t find “those questions” necessary for good fantasy fiction: take a hint from JK Rowling, whose whole story revolves around witches and wizards, yet she never says anything negative about religion. Seriously, Mr. Delaney: <i>If you don’t have anything nice to say, don’t say anything at all!</i> Now granted, I like stories that are about that cosmic, seemingly-metaphorical “Light/Dark” battle, but could we please not get religion-specific? Or at least, leave the religion-specific stuff to people like Ted Dekker and Frank Peretti who actually know what they’re talking about? Please?! Oh well, it may sound like I’m ragging on the series, but I really do like it! I’m definitely hooked at this point! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7850572529782271420" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1235595500" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1235595500" />
    <a title="Michael Weber-Williams" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38963637-michael-weber-williams"><img alt="Michael Weber-Williams" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1235595500?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Weber-Williams" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Weber-Williams" href="/user/show/38963637-michael-weber-williams">Michael Weber-Williams</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1235595500" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17775423021334020760"><br/>"I see your future clearly. Your life will be sad. Your master will be dead and you will be alone. It would be better if you had never been born." --Tibb<br/><br/><br/> In The Last Apprentice: Attack of the Fiend, the fourth book in The Last Apprentice Series, Tomas Ward continues his apprenticeship with his master, John Gregory, and ironic witch friend, Alice Deane. In the last book, Tom’s father past away, his mother returned to her homeland, and their oldest son, Jack, inherited the farm, except for one roo</span>
  <span id="freeText17775423021334020760" style="display:none"><br />"I see your future clearly. Your life will be sad. Your master will be dead and you will be alone. It would be better if you had never been born." --Tibb<br /><br /><br /> In The Last Apprentice: Attack of the Fiend, the fourth book in The Last Apprentice Series, Tomas Ward continues his apprenticeship with his master, John Gregory, and ironic witch friend, Alice Deane. In the last book, Tom’s father past away, his mother returned to her homeland, and their oldest son, Jack, inherited the farm, except for one room. This room, along with everything in it, was willed to Tom and only he was allowed in it. One day, the Spook allowed him and Alice to return home and retrieve the contents of the room; however, when they arrived, the house was empty and ransacked. In addition, the items Tom was sent to obtain were stolen. Alice was able to detect the scent of witches and started off in the direction of a witch infested city: Pendle. At about the same time, John received a visit from a priest and prior apprentice from the city named Father Stocks. He informed the Spook about how the three clans that roamed Pendle --Deanes, Malkins, and Moulderheels-- were rumored to be growing and uniting to conjure an immeasurable evil. Hearing this, John and Tom sent out for Pendle.<br /><br /><br /> Once at Pendle, Thomas and his master resided with Father Stocks in the presbytery in the town of Downham. While Father Stocks and the Spook were out, Tom received a visit from a girl named Mab. She said that Alice was captured and put under a spell and needed help. Tom followed Mab into a clearing where he encountered Mab’s twin sisters: Beth and Jennet. There he was seated on a stump and noticed some oddities about the girls. Eventually, Thomas determined that they witches! As he tried to stand and face the sisters, Tom Ward realized that he was unable to stand or move his body at all. Due to his entrapment, the young witches decided to have a little fun and play “Truth or Dare.” Will Tom be able to break free? Will he be able to rescue Alice and his family? What is to become of the witch covens? There’s only one way of finding out!<br /><br /><br /> The book takes place in a undetermined place and time of old. Throughout the book Thomas struggles with trying to concoct a way to save his closest, remaining family. Along the way he learns that if he puts his mind to something, he is capable of anything. Sometimes in life, if you focus and dedicate yourself to a cause, you will see it fulfilled. I chose to read this book because I have read the three first books in the series and highly enjoyed them. As I was hoping, this book was just like its predecessors. The Last Apprentice: Attack of the Fiend kept me enthralled and definitely held up to its promise. These books remind me of my life because, in the series, Tom Ward has issues with his family. Since he is training to become a Spook and deals with the darkness, they kind of don’t want much to do with him. With my situation, my stepdad was laid off and we could no longer make a living in Colorado creating a tough decision for my stepsisters. They could have either moved here with us or stay in Colorado with their mother. They ended up choosing the latter. Ever since then, the older of the two hasn’t said a word to us or even tried to contact us. Jack, Tom’s eldest brother, and his wife Ellie aren’t as standoffish, but they do try to keep their distance to avoid any issues with the dark. Ironically, the opposite happened in this book.<br /><br /><br /> You should read The Last Apprentice: Attack of the Fiend if you want an easy, enjoyable mystery that is as humorous as it is thrilling. You won’t be able to set it down! This book is intended for people who are intrigued by supernatural beings and folklore, but anyone who appreciates a breathtaking and gripping novel will also love it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17775423021334020760" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zB7Aa8U6Ws8LGA4xE4US5OQpIqaoQvjagIVdwAxtT+z5EjhVfDcFM6RC33U+HhrgG3MkOfmz3s+bTjvPoRGrmA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/146374.Joseph_Delaney">About Joseph Delaney</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/146374.Joseph_Delaney"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1376358484p3/146374.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/146374.Joseph_Delaney">Joseph Delaney

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12716529966612275300">Joseph Delaney is a full time writer living in Lancashire, in the heart of Boggart territory.<br/>He is the author of Wardstone Chronicles, Starblade Chronicles, Arena 13, Aberrations and a new book came out in April 2020, Brother Wulf. This is a new spooks story featuring Tom and Alice, but introducing a new character, a young monk called Brother Wulf. <br/><br/>He first got the idea for the Spooks series when </span>
  <span id="freeText12716529966612275300" style="display:none">Joseph Delaney is a full time writer living in Lancashire, in the heart of Boggart territory.<br />He is the author of Wardstone Chronicles, Starblade Chronicles, Arena 13, Aberrations and a new book came out in April 2020, Brother Wulf. This is a new spooks story featuring Tom and Alice, but introducing a new character, a young monk called Brother Wulf. <br /><br />He first got the idea for the Spooks series when he moved to the village where he lives now and discovered there was a local boggart - ‘a man like me needs boggarts around’. He made a note in his notebook ‘a story about a man who hunts boggarts’ and years later when he had to come up with an idea at short notice developed this into ‘The Spook’s Apprentice’, the first book in the series.<br />He continues to draw upon the folklore of Lancashire and has acquired much local knowledge over the years which he tweaks and modifies to create his fictional world. Another source of inspiration has been Lancashire's varied and atmospheric landscape. Many of the locations in the County are based on actual places in Lancashire. <br />In the early days of his writing career Joseph worked as a teacher at a Sixth Form College: his subjects were English, Film and Media Studies. He used to get up early and write every morning before work. That way he could write a book a year – which promptly got rejected! When the Americans bought the series he decided to give up teaching and write full time. <br />Prior to teaching he worked as an engineer in his twenties, completing an apprenticeship just like Tom Ward in the spook’s books.<br />Joseph describes his method of writing as a process of discovery. He doesn’t plot too far ahead and often doesn’t know what is going to happen until he writes it down. In other words he makes it up as he goes along. He prefers writing dialogue to description, in which he says he is a minimalist and leaves much to the reader’s imagination. <br />Joseph has three children and nine grandchildren and is a wonderful public speaker available for conference, library and bookshop events.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2330711.The_Spook_s_Apprentice" title="The Spook's Apprentice" rel="nofollow noopener">The Spook's Apprentice</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17426629.The_Spook_s_Curse" title="The Spook's Curse" rel="nofollow noopener">The Spook's Curse</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17426189.The_Spook_s_Secret" title="The Spook's Secret" rel="nofollow noopener">The Spook's Secret</a> have all been shortlisted for the Lancashire children's Book for the Year Award. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2330711.The_Spook_s_Apprentice" title="The Spook's Apprentice" rel="nofollow noopener">The Spook's Apprentice</a> is the winner of both the Sefton Book Award and the Hampshire Book Award.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.josephdelaneyauthor.com">www.josephdelaneyauthor.com</a><br /><br /><br /><i>from <a href="http://www.rbooks.co.uk/author.aspx?id=15205" rel="nofollow noopener">publisher's website</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="12716529966612275300" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
